<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Alternative_metal" title="Alternative metal">alternative metal</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Instrument(s)</th><td class="infobox-data note"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist">

<li>guitar</li>
<li>keyboards</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><span class="nowrap">Years active</span></th><td class="infobox-data">1994–present</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Labels</th><td class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Machine_Shop_Records" title="Machine Shop Records">Machine Shop</a></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros.</a></span></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Member of</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Formerly of</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Fort_Minor" title="Fort Minor">Fort Minor</a></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mikeshinoda.com">mikeshinoda<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header">Signature</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Mike_Shinoda%27s_signature.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Mike_Shinoda%27s_signature.svg/150px-Mike_Shinoda%27s_signature.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="138" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Mike_Shinoda%27s_signature.svg/225px-Mike_Shinoda%27s_signature.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Mike_Shinoda%27s_signature.svg/300px-Mike_Shinoda%27s_signature.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="471" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Michael Kenji Shinoda</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ʃ/: &#39;sh&#39; in &#39;shy&#39;">ʃ</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born February 11, 1977) is an American musician, singer, rapper, songwriter, and record producer. He co-founded the rock band <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a> in 1996 and is the band's co-lead vocalist, as well as rhythm guitarist, keyboardist, primary songwriter and producer. Shinoda later created a hip-hop-driven side project, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Minor" title="Fort Minor">Fort Minor</a>, in 2004. He has also served as a producer for tracks and albums by artists such as <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Styles_of_Beyond" title="Styles of Beyond">Styles of Beyond</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_X-Ecutioners" title="The X-Ecutioners">the X-Ecutioners</a>.
</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Panorama_City,_Los_Angeles" title="Panorama City, Los Angeles">Panorama City, Los Angeles</a>, California, and raised in <a href="/wiki/Agoura_Hills,_California" title="Agoura Hills, California">Agoura Hills</a>, Shinoda formed Xero, which later became Linkin Park, with two of his high school friends: <a href="/wiki/Brad_Delson" title="Brad Delson">Brad Delson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Bourdon" title="Rob Bourdon">Rob Bourdon</a> in 1996, later joined by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Hahn" title="Joe Hahn">Joe Hahn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Farrell" title="Dave Farrell">Dave Farrell</a> and Mark Wakefield. <a href="/wiki/Chester_Bennington" title="Chester Bennington">Chester Bennington</a> joined Linkin Park in 1999, replacing Wakefield as lead vocalist. The band later signed a record deal with Warner Bros Records.
</p><p>Shinoda is also the co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Machine_Shop_Records" title="Machine Shop Records">Machine Shop Records</a>, a California-based record label. Outside of music, Shinoda is an artist and graphic designer. He has painted several pieces of artwork, some of which have been featured in the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_American_National_Museum" title="Japanese American National Museum">Japanese American National Museum</a>. In 2018, Shinoda released his debut solo album <i><a href="/wiki/Post_Traumatic" title="Post Traumatic">Post Traumatic</a></i>, which consists of 18 songs about his feelings following the death of his Linkin Park bandmate Bennington.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Michael Kenji Shinoda (<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span lang="ja">篠田 賢治</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Japanese" title="Romanization of Japanese">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><span title="Japanese-language romanization"><i lang="ja-Latn">Shinoda Kenji</i></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> was born on February 11, 1977, in <a href="/wiki/Panorama_City,_Los_Angeles" title="Panorama City, Los Angeles">Panorama City, California</a>, and raised in <a href="/wiki/Agoura_Hills,_California" title="Agoura Hills, California">Agoura Hills, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MetalHammerInterview_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetalHammerInterview-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> His father is <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Americans" title="Japanese Americans">Japanese-American</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> he has a younger brother named Jason,<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and he was raised as a liberal <a href="/wiki/Mainline_Protestant" title="Mainline Protestant">Protestant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda's mother encouraged him to take classical piano lessons when he was six. By 13, he expressed the desire to move toward playing <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He later added the guitar and rap-style vocals to his repertoire during his middle school and high school years.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MetalHammerInterview_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetalHammerInterview-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shinoda attended <a href="/wiki/Agoura_High_School" title="Agoura High School">Agoura High School</a> with future Linkin Park bandmates <a href="/wiki/Brad_Delson" title="Brad Delson">Brad Delson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Bourdon" title="Rob Bourdon">Rob Bourdon</a>. The three formed the band Xero, and began to make a more serious attempt to pursue a career in the music industry. After graduating high school, Shinoda enrolled in the <a href="/wiki/Art_Center_College_of_Design" class="mw-redirect" title="Art Center College of Design">Art Center College of Design</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena</a> to study <a href="/wiki/Graphic_design" title="Graphic design">graphic design</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illustration" title="Illustration">illustration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He attended classes with DJ and <a href="/wiki/Turntablist" class="mw-redirect" title="Turntablist">turntablist</a> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Hahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Hahn">Joseph Hahn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> While studying at the Art Center College of Design, he experienced a form of <a href="/wiki/Identity_crisis_(psychology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Identity crisis (psychology)">identity crisis</a>. Years later, he told an interviewer:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I think it was probably in college that I realized that there was a difference between Japanese and Japanese-American. That's important to realize. It's not the same thing and then eventually with Linkin Park, I toured in Japan. I've been there now I think four times. I remember the first time I went, how familiar it seemed, just getting out of the plane, it smelled like my aunt's house, in the airport, it smelled like Japan. I don't know if anybody else even noticed it but I walked out of the plane and thought this is definitely familiar to me, didn't even see anything yet. And then going to Tokyo, <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyoto" title="Kyoto">Kyoto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagoya" title="Nagoya">Nagoya</a>, you just recognize things about the way people act, the small things that people do such as how you'll grab a piece of paper. There are things that are more obvious like taking somebody's business card with two hands. You don't do that in the States. When I saw somebody do that I went, "Oh yeah, my uncle always does that," you know. There are little things that culturally come from Japan but they also exist in Japanese American culture and it made me feel like the connection was there and I kind of hadn't realized how much of it was there.<sup id="cite_ref-roots_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roots-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Shinoda graduated in 1998 with a Bachelor of Arts in Illustration and obtained a job as a graphic designer.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Linkin_Park">Linkin Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Linkin Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a></div>
<p>Shinoda founded Linkin Park with <a href="/wiki/Rob_Bourdon" title="Rob Bourdon">Rob Bourdon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brad_Delson" title="Brad Delson">Brad Delson</a> in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-Ask-Bio_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ask-Bio-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> They eventually brought in turntablist <a href="/wiki/Joe_Hahn" title="Joe Hahn">Joe Hahn</a>, bassist <a href="/wiki/Dave_Farrell" title="Dave Farrell">Dave Farrell</a>, and vocalist Mark Wakefield. The earliest incarnation of the band was called Xero. The band was limited in resources and originally produced and recorded music in Shinoda's bedroom, which resulted in the release of a four-track demo tape, entitled <i>Xero</i>, in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stone1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stone1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> When the band was unable to find a record deal, Wakefield and Farrell left the band to pursue other musical interests, though Farrell's departure turned out to be temporary. The band later recruited <a href="/wiki/Chester_Bennington" title="Chester Bennington">Chester Bennington</a> and successfully landed a record deal with Warner Bros Records. Linkin Park's first studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Hybrid_Theory" title="Hybrid Theory">Hybrid Theory</a></i> went on to become a breakthrough success and helped the band attain international success.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_5-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stone1_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stone1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shinoda is closely involved in the technical aspects of the band's recordings, and over the subsequent releases that role continued to expand. Shinoda, with guitarist <a href="/wiki/Brad_Delson" title="Brad Delson">Brad Delson</a>, engineered and produced the band's <i><a href="/wiki/Hybrid_Theory_(EP)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hybrid Theory (EP)">Hybrid Theory EP</a></i>, and performed similar roles in the recording of <i><a href="/wiki/Hybrid_Theory" title="Hybrid Theory">Hybrid Theory</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-band_bio_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-band_bio-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He has contributed to the instrumental and lyrical composition on most of Linkin Park's songs. Though Bennington primarily served as Linkin Park's lead vocalist, he occasionally shared the role with Shinoda.<sup id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_2002_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_2002-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Bennington had a higher pitched and emotional style of singing,<sup id="cite_ref-mtv1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> whereas Shinoda has a baritone hip-hop style delivery.<sup id="cite_ref-hp_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hp-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda organized and oversaw the band's first remix album <a href="/wiki/Reanimation_(Linkin_Park_album)" title="Reanimation (Linkin Park album)"><i>Reanimation</i></a> in 2002, contributing his own production of remixes that he made in his home studio for "<a href="/wiki/Crawling_(song)" title="Crawling (song)">Crawling</a>" and "Pushing Me Away". Shinoda collaborated with graffiti artist DELTA, graphic designer Frank Maddocks, and bandmate <a href="/wiki/Joe_Hahn" title="Joe Hahn">Joe Hahn</a> to prepare <i>Reanimation</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s artwork. Mike also collaborated with the Flem, Delta, James R. Minchin III, Nick Spanos, and Joe Hahn for the artwork of the band's second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Meteora_(album)" title="Meteora (album)">Meteora</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda also produced the album, with his bandmates and Don Gilmore which was his first production experience. By the release of the <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and Linkin Park collaborative mashup EP, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Collision_Course_(EP)" title="Collision Course (EP)">Collision Course</a></i> in 2004, Shinoda's involvement in the creation of the albums continued to grow.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He produced and mixed the album, which won a Grammy Award for "best rap / song collaboration" in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Grammy2006_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy2006-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mike_Shinoda_World_Expo_2008.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Mike_Shinoda_World_Expo_2008.jpg/220px-Mike_Shinoda_World_Expo_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Mike_Shinoda_World_Expo_2008.jpg/330px-Mike_Shinoda_World_Expo_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Mike_Shinoda_World_Expo_2008.jpg/440px-Mike_Shinoda_World_Expo_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a><figcaption>Shinoda at <a href="/wiki/Expo_2008" title="Expo 2008">World Expo</a> 2008</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mike_Shinoda,_Linkin_Park_@_Sonisphere_2009.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Mike_Shinoda%2C_Linkin_Park_%40_Sonisphere_2009.jpg/170px-Mike_Shinoda%2C_Linkin_Park_%40_Sonisphere_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="280" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Mike_Shinoda%2C_Linkin_Park_%40_Sonisphere_2009.jpg/255px-Mike_Shinoda%2C_Linkin_Park_%40_Sonisphere_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Mike_Shinoda%2C_Linkin_Park_%40_Sonisphere_2009.jpg/340px-Mike_Shinoda%2C_Linkin_Park_%40_Sonisphere_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1092" data-file-height="1800" /></a><figcaption>Shinoda performing at Sonisphere Festival in Kirjurinluoto, Pori, Finland, 2009</figcaption></figure>
<p>The band released their next album, <i>Minutes to Midnight</i>, on May 14, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> On this album, Shinoda shared a production credit with longtime producer <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">Rick Rubin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> This album was also the first time that Shinoda, best known for his rapping, sang a featured vocal (even though he sang backing vocals for their previous two albums). Shinoda sang in the songs "In Between" and the B-side song, "No Roads Left", as well as rapping and singing in the songs "Bleed It Out" and "Hands Held High".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Despite the rarity of Shinoda-fronted singing tracks, music magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Hit_Parader" title="Hit Parader">Hit Parader</a></i> ranked him at number 72 of the Top 100 Metal Vocalists of All Time.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shinoda and Rubin again shared a production credit for Linkin Park's fourth album, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Thousand_Suns" title="A Thousand Suns">A Thousand Suns</a></i>, which was released on September 14, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> This album featured more of his singing than rapping. Shinoda raps in three tracks, specifically "When They Come for Me", "Wretches and Kings" and second single "<a href="/wiki/Waiting_for_the_End_(Linkin_Park_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Waiting for the End (Linkin Park song)">Waiting for the End</a>", while he sings on numerous songs (specifically verses), such as third single "<a href="/wiki/Burning_in_the_Skies" title="Burning in the Skies">Burning in the Skies</a>", "Robot Boy", "<a href="/wiki/Blackout_(Linkin_Park_song)" title="Blackout (Linkin Park song)">Blackout</a>", fourth single "<a href="/wiki/Iridescent_(song)" title="Iridescent (song)">Iridescent</a>" and lead single "<a href="/wiki/The_Catalyst" title="The Catalyst">The Catalyst</a>". Bennington and Shinoda sang simultaneously together on "The Catalyst", "Jornada del Muerto" and "Robot Boy", while "Iridescent" features all band members singing together.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Linkin Park released their fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Living_Things_(Linkin_Park_album)" title="Living Things (Linkin Park album)">Living Things</a></i>, on June 26, 2012. This album was stated as more "rap-centric" by Shinoda compared to the previous two albums.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Whereas there were tracks like "Skin to Bone", "Roads Untraveled" and "<a href="/wiki/Castle_of_Glass" title="Castle of Glass">Castle of Glass</a>" which featured the singing vocals by Shinoda and had <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a>, influenced by the works of <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>, as well as the inspirations of Dylan.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Allmusic described Shinoda's work for the album as, "a fitting soundtrack for aging rap-rockers who are comfortable in their skin but restless at heart".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Recharged_(Linkin_Park_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Recharged (Linkin Park album)">Recharged</a></i>, which is a remix album consisting remixes of original songs from <i>Living Things</i>, was released on October 29, 2013. Shinoda used his <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Dance_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic Dance Music">EDM</a> experience he got from <a href="/wiki/Avicii" title="Avicii">Avicii</a> while working on the track "<a href="/wiki/Wake_Me_Up_(Avicii_song)" title="Wake Me Up (Avicii song)">Wake Me Up</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> and also from <a href="/wiki/Steve_Aoki" title="Steve Aoki">Steve Aoki</a> while working on "<a href="/wiki/A_Light_That_Never_Comes" title="A Light That Never Comes">A Light That Never Comes</a>", to remix some songs for the album.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda reinterpreted songs like "Castle of Glass" and "Victimized". He also worked with his old friends like DJ Vice and <a href="/wiki/Styles_of_Beyond" title="Styles of Beyond">Ryu</a> for the album.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, Shinoda worked with Delson to produce the band's sixth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunting_Party_(album)" title="The Hunting Party (album)">The Hunting Party</a></i>, which was released on June 17, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The album is the first one to have featuring artists like <a href="/wiki/Page_Hamilton" title="Page Hamilton">Page Hamilton</a> of <a href="/wiki/Helmet_(band)" title="Helmet (band)">Helmet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rakim" title="Rakim">Rakim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daron_Malakian" title="Daron Malakian">Daron Malakian</a> of <a href="/wiki/System_of_a_Down" title="System of a Down">System of a Down</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Morello" title="Tom Morello">Tom Morello</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rage_Against_the_Machine" title="Rage Against the Machine">Rage Against the Machine</a>. The first single of the album, "<a href="/wiki/Guilty_All_the_Same" title="Guilty All the Same">Guilty All the Same</a>", is the first non-remix song by the band to feature rap by a guest artist instead of Shinoda.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The pre-production of their seventh studio album began in mid-2015 during <a href="/wiki/The_Hunting_Party_Tour" title="The Hunting Party Tour">The Hunting Party Tour</a> by Shinoda on his phone.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, Shinoda again worked with Delson on the production of <i><a href="/wiki/One_More_Light" title="One More Light">One More Light</a></i>. The album is the first to feature other songwriters rather than the band itself. The album overall includes singing from Shinoda, but a few songs have rap in them. "<a href="/wiki/Good_Goodbye" title="Good Goodbye">Good Goodbye</a>" is a song that features rapping from Shinoda, <a href="/wiki/Stormzy" title="Stormzy">Stormzy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pusha_T" title="Pusha T">Pusha T</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fort_Minor">Fort Minor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Fort Minor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fort_Minor" title="Fort Minor">Fort Minor</a></div>
<p>In 2004, Shinoda formed a <a href="/wiki/Side_project" title="Side project">side project</a> called Fort Minor, which he used as an avenue to further showcase his hip-hop background. He explained the origin of the project's name in an interview stating,<sup id="cite_ref-am1_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-am1-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>'Fort' represents the more aggressive side of the music. 'Minor' can mean a few things: if you're talking about <a href="/wiki/Music_theory" title="Music theory">music theory</a>, the minor key is darker. I wanted to name the album rather than having my name on the cover, because I want people to focus on the music, not me.<sup id="cite_ref-am1_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-am1-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Shinoda began recording songs for this side project following the release of <a href="/wiki/Collision_Course_(EP)" title="Collision Course (EP)">Collision Course</a> in November 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Fort_Minor:_We_Major" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Minor: We Major">Fort Minor: We Major</a></i> was a <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> by Shinoda and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Green_Lantern" title="DJ Green Lantern">DJ Green Lantern</a> to promote his upcoming studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rising_Tied" title="The Rising Tied">The Rising Tied</a></i>, the debut album of Fort Minor, was released in November 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-rovi_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rovi-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Robert Hales directed its first video "<a href="/wiki/Petrified/Remember_the_Name" class="mw-redirect" title="Petrified/Remember the Name">Petrified</a>", which was released the previous month.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mike_Shinoda_4.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Mike_Shinoda_4.jpg/220px-Mike_Shinoda_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Mike_Shinoda_4.jpg/330px-Mike_Shinoda_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Mike_Shinoda_4.jpg/440px-Mike_Shinoda_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="401" /></a><figcaption>Shinoda performing live, 2008</figcaption></figure>
<p>Fort Minor's debut album, titled <i>The Rising Tied</i>, was released on November 22, 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-rovi_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rovi-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The album featured musical collaborations from Styles of Beyond, <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_(rapper)" title="Common (rapper)">Common</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Thought" title="Black Thought">Black Thought</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">the Roots</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holly_Brook" class="mw-redirect" title="Holly Brook">Holly Brook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonah_Matranga" title="Jonah Matranga">Jonah Matranga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Celph_Titled" title="Celph Titled">Celph Titled</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rovi_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rovi-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-build_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-build-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, who had previously collaborated with Linkin Park on the 2004 album <i><a href="/wiki/Collision_Course_(EP)" title="Collision Course (EP)">Collision Course</a></i>, also served as the album's executive producer.<sup id="cite_ref-rovi_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rovi-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-build_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-build-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda told Corey Moss of <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> that he imposed on himself a requirement to play all the instruments and write all the lyrics to the album, except for the strings, percussion, or choir parts.<sup id="cite_ref-Storyteller_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Storyteller-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Rising Tied</i> was positively received by critics. The album's most successful single, "<a href="/wiki/Where%27d_You_Go_(Fort_Minor_song)" title="Where&#39;d You Go (Fort Minor song)">Where'd You Go</a>", peaked at #4 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Billboard Hot 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-single_charts_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-single_charts-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wheredyougopos_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wheredyougopos-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Other songs like, "Petrified" and "<a href="/wiki/Remember_the_Name" title="Remember the Name">Remember the Name</a>" gained popularity when they were used as the soundtrack for <a href="/wiki/NBA_on_TNT" title="NBA on TNT">NBA Overtime</a> on <a href="/wiki/TNT_(U.S._TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="TNT (U.S. TV network)">TNT</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Another track, "Kenji", describes the experiences of a Japanese-American family during the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_American_internment" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese American internment">Japanese American internment</a> of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rising_Tied_allmusic_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rising_Tied_allmusic-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the success of "Where'd You Go" during the week of April 26, 2006, sales of <i>The Rising Tied</i> increased by 45 percent, and the album chart position went up 89 positions to No. 104 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200."<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> "Where'd You Go" was awarded Ringtone of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/2006_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2006 MTV Video Music Awards">2006 MTV Video Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In mid August 2006 Fort Minor performed at the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Sonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Sonic">Summer Sonic</a> 2006 alongside Linkin Park.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2006, Fort Minor released a video for "Where'd You Go." Shinoda has stated he felt the video was a nice wrap-up for Fort Minor. Also in November, Shinoda stated that Fort Minor would go on an indefinite hiatus, because of his dedication to Linkin Park. In the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> One-hit Wonders of the 2000s, Fort Minor (along with Holly Brook and Jonah Matranga) were listed at No.&#160;19, due to the success of "Where'd You Go" (since it was Fort Minor's only single that reached the top 25).<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In an interview in 2014, Shinoda stated that there could be a possible Fort Minor album in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 21, 2015, Shinoda officially confirmed Fort Minor's return with a status update and the release of a new single, "<a href="/wiki/Welcome_(Fort_Minor_song)" title="Welcome (Fort Minor song)">Welcome</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Fort Minor also appeared as the musical guest on the <a href="/wiki/TBS_(U.S._TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="TBS (U.S. TV channel)">TBS</a> late-night talk show <i><a href="/wiki/Conan_(talk_show)" title="Conan (talk show)">Conan</a></i> on Monday, June 22.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Fort Minor also appeared on a few shows during Linkin Park's touring schedule.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solo_work">Solo work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Solo work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On January 25, 2018, Shinoda released the <i><a href="/wiki/Post_Traumatic_(EP)" title="Post Traumatic (EP)">Post Traumatic</a></i> EP,  featuring three songs about his own feelings in the aftermath of Chester Bennington's death on July 20, 2017. Shinoda released the EP under his own name instead of under his side-project, Fort Minor.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 8, 2018, Shinoda announced through social media that he was working on a new solo album. He also added that he was in Los Angeles filming a music video and also invited fans to appear in the video, including a map of the old Tower Records in Hollywood, California.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda performed in Los Angeles on May 12 as part of Identity LA, marking one of his first performances since Bennington's death.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> On March 28, 2018, the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Reading_%26_Leeds_Festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Reading &amp; Leeds Festivals">Reading &amp; Leeds Festivals</a> roster was announced, with Shinoda included. He performed on August 25 and 26 as part of the Reading &amp; Leeds Festivals, joining artists and bands such as <a href="/wiki/Post_Malone" title="Post Malone">Post Malone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panic!_at_the_Disco" title="Panic! at the Disco">Panic! at the Disco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dua_Lipa" title="Dua Lipa">Dua Lipa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brockhampton_(band)" title="Brockhampton (band)">Brockhampton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott" title="Travis Scott">Travis Scott</a>; <a href="/wiki/Fall_Out_Boy" title="Fall Out Boy">Fall Out Boy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kings_of_Leon" title="Kings of Leon">Kings of Leon</a> were headlining the event.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The next day, Shinoda released two new songs, "Crossing a Line" and "Nothing Makes Sense Anymore," from his upcoming studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Post_Traumatic_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Post Traumatic (album)">Post Traumatic</a></i> which was released on June 15.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> On March 29, 2018, Shinoda did an interview with KROQ where his single “Crossing a Line” was debuted on the radio.<sup id="cite_ref-kroq-solo_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kroq-solo-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On April 26, 2018, Shinoda released a song, "About You," featuring hip hop artist, <a href="/wiki/Blackbear_(musician)" title="Blackbear (musician)">Blackbear</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> About a month later he revealed that he would be releasing a new song called "Running From My Shadow" which featured <a href="/wiki/Grandson_(musician)" title="Grandson (musician)">Grandson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Another single was released just a few weeks after "Running From My Shadow" was released. The new single, "Ghosts", was released on June 7, 2018, 6 days before the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Post_Traumatic" title="Post Traumatic">Post Traumatic</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 30, 2019, Shinoda announced that he would be releasing a new single, "Fine," two days later, on November 1.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2020, Shinoda began sharing new musical content by live streaming from his home studio. He called these tracks, <i>CoronaJams</i>, after the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda later released these tracks over three separate albums beginning in July: <i><a href="/wiki/Dropped_Frames,_Vol._1" class="mw-redirect" title="Dropped Frames, Vol. 1">Dropped Frames, Vol. 1</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dropped Frames, Vol. 2</i>, and <i>Dropped Frames, Vol. 3</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 19, 2021, Shinoda released a single titled "Happy Endings". The song features guest vocals from <a href="/wiki/Iann_Dior" title="Iann Dior">Iann Dior</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upsahl" title="Upsahl">Upsahl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda also remixed the <a href="/wiki/Deftones" title="Deftones">Deftones</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Passenger_(Deftones_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Passenger (Deftones song)">Passenger</a>" which earned him a Grammy at the <a href="/wiki/64th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="64th Annual Grammy Awards">2022 Grammy Awards</a> for the category of <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Remixed_Recording,_Non-Classical" title="Grammy Award for Best Remixed Recording, Non-Classical">Grammy Award for Best Remixed Recording, Non-Classical</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> On March 10, 2023, in the midst of re-releasing Linkin Park's <i>Meteora</i> to celebrate its 20th anniversary, Shinoda released a new solo single titled "In My Head" as part of the soundtrack to the film <i><a href="/wiki/Scream_VI" title="Scream VI">Scream VI</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Pop_rock" title="Pop rock">pop rock</a> song contains a feature appearance from <a href="/wiki/Kailee_Morgue" title="Kailee Morgue">Kailee Morgue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda also produced and co-wrote "Still Alive", a song recorded by <a href="/wiki/Demi_Lovato" title="Demi Lovato">Demi Lovato</a> which also appears in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_painting">Art and painting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Art and painting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Concert_of_Mike_Shinoda_at_the_Z%C3%A9nith_de_Paris_IMG_20190309_220810_(46437672695).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Concert_of_Mike_Shinoda_at_the_Z%C3%A9nith_de_Paris_IMG_20190309_220810_%2846437672695%29.jpg/200px-Concert_of_Mike_Shinoda_at_the_Z%C3%A9nith_de_Paris_IMG_20190309_220810_%2846437672695%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Concert_of_Mike_Shinoda_at_the_Z%C3%A9nith_de_Paris_IMG_20190309_220810_%2846437672695%29.jpg/300px-Concert_of_Mike_Shinoda_at_the_Z%C3%A9nith_de_Paris_IMG_20190309_220810_%2846437672695%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Concert_of_Mike_Shinoda_at_the_Z%C3%A9nith_de_Paris_IMG_20190309_220810_%2846437672695%29.jpg/400px-Concert_of_Mike_Shinoda_at_the_Z%C3%A9nith_de_Paris_IMG_20190309_220810_%2846437672695%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a><figcaption>Shinoda performing live, Zénith de Paris, 2019</figcaption></figure>
<p>Shinoda has had a hand in most artistic facets of <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a>'s imagery, including the group's album artwork, band merchandise, web design, and on-stage production art.<sup id="cite_ref-art1_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art1-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> He designed the cover art for <a href="/wiki/Styles_of_Beyond" title="Styles of Beyond">Styles of Beyond</a>'s debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/2000_Fold" title="2000 Fold">2000 Fold</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saukrates" title="Saukrates">Saukrates</a>' debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Underground_Tapes" title="The Underground Tapes">The Underground Tapes</a></i>, and DJ Frane's debut album, <i>Frane's Fantastic Boatride</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> all released in 1999. He has also worked on several art projects throughout his career.
</p><p>In 2003, he did a collaborative "remix" shoe for <a href="/wiki/DC_Shoes" title="DC Shoes">DC Shoes</a>, remixing the "Clientele". He reworked the colors and materials for the shoe, and additionally designed all the packaging and print advertisements.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The following year, he also designed a customization of a <a href="/wiki/Kid_Robot" class="mw-redirect" title="Kid Robot">Kid Robot</a> "Munny" doll for a charity auction.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Later in 2008, Shinoda partnered with DC Shoes again on a second DC Remix Series project. The new collaboration featured a "great juxtaposition of Shinoda's unique influences: accomplished artist versus recording-breaking musician, American upbringing versus Japanese heritage." The MS/DC limited edition remix has two different versions – Xander and Pride. Roughly 2000 pairs of the limited edition shoes were made available for purchase when the sneaker was released on August 1, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, Shinoda created a series of ten paintings which became the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Fort_Minor" title="Fort Minor">Fort Minor</a> debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rising_Tied" title="The Rising Tied">The Rising Tied</a></i>. That series became the backbone for the packaging of the album, and was featured in Shinoda's first public art show "Diamonds Spades Hearts &amp; Clubs".<sup id="cite_ref-Fort_Minor_Official_Website_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fort_Minor_Official_Website-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the ten Fort Minor pieces, the show also featured thirteen more original works and five collaborative pieces. "Diamonds Spades Hearts &amp; Clubs" opened at Gallery 1988 on Sunday, November 19, 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, Shinoda founded a college scholarship at <a href="/wiki/Art_Center_College_of_Design" class="mw-redirect" title="Art Center College of Design">Art Center College of Design</a> to benefit future illustration and graphic design students. Named the Michael K. Shinoda Endowed Scholarship, it is awarded based on financial need and merit. The scholarship was awarded for the first time in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The scholarship fund is made possible through the sale of his original artwork on his website, art shows and his DC Shoes projects.<sup id="cite_ref-Fort_Minor_Official_Website_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fort_Minor_Official_Website-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mike_Shinoda_Official_Store_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mike_Shinoda_Official_Store-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 11, 2008, Shinoda's second public art show "Glorious Excess (BORN)" premiered at the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_American_National_Museum" title="Japanese American National Museum">Japanese American National Museum</a> in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-thehawaiiherald_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thehawaiiherald-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The show included nine new pieces, with an exclusive signing on opening night.<sup id="cite_ref-thehawaiiherald_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thehawaiiherald-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The show served as part one of the two-part "Glorious Excess" series, with the second installment "Glorious Excess (DIES)" due at JANM on August 22, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda commented on the inspiration behind the <i>Glorious Excess</i> series, stating, "It Got to a point where the pervasiveness of 'celebrity news' concerned me. It seemed like it has jumped out of its niche into places where it doesn't belong. I would be watching the news, and thinking, 'of all the things going on in the world right now, why are they covering so-and-so's breakup?' It didn't make sense to me. Add to that the fact that I'm supposed to somehow 'belong' to that celebrity group—and I really don't feel like I do in a lot of ways—and you can see how the topic started to become really interesting to me. The Glorious Excess (BORN) show was my way of diving into those topics, trying to find answers. It follows a central 'celebrity' character, who is filthy rich, slightly violent, and famous without any particular skill or talent."<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 6, 2014, Shinoda and Hahn painted an artwork on the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_musical_activities">Other musical activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other musical activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mike_Shinoda_at_Soundwave_2013.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Mike_Shinoda_at_Soundwave_2013.jpg/220px-Mike_Shinoda_at_Soundwave_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Mike_Shinoda_at_Soundwave_2013.jpg/330px-Mike_Shinoda_at_Soundwave_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Mike_Shinoda_at_Soundwave_2013.jpg/440px-Mike_Shinoda_at_Soundwave_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2836" data-file-height="1983" /></a><figcaption>Shinoda performing at Soundwave in 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>Shinoda has also served as a music producer for several other artists and groups. In 2002, Shinoda and Joe Hahn collaborated with the <a href="/wiki/X-Ecutioners" class="mw-redirect" title="X-Ecutioners">X-Ecutioners</a> to produce and perform on their single "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Goin%27_Down_(X-Ecutioners_song)" title="It&#39;s Goin&#39; Down (X-Ecutioners song)">It's Goin' Down</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Later in 2002, Shinoda and Brad Delson established their own record label, <a href="/wiki/Machine_Shop_Recordings" class="mw-redirect" title="Machine Shop Recordings">Machine Shop Recordings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-msr_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msr-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> He helped produce <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a>'s 2006 release,<i> <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco%27s_Food_%26_Liquor" title="Lupe Fiasco&#39;s Food &amp; Liquor">Food &amp; Liquor</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> He extensively worked with <a href="/wiki/Styles_of_Beyond" title="Styles of Beyond">Styles of Beyond</a> between 2009 and 2012 to help produce <i>Reseda Beach</i>, which also features his instrumental and vocal contribution.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In addition albums, Shinoda scored the <a href="/wiki/MTV_VMA" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV VMA">MTV VMA</a>'s in 2005 and also worked with <a href="/wiki/Ramin_Djawadi" title="Ramin Djawadi">Ramin Djawadi</a> to score the video game, <i><a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor:_Warfighter" title="Medal of Honor: Warfighter">Medal of Honor: Warfighter</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, he collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Trapanese" title="Joseph Trapanese">Joseph Trapanese</a> to compose the score for the American release of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Raid:_Redemption" class="mw-redirect" title="The Raid: Redemption">The Raid: Redemption</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, he released a remixed single and animated music video of the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Depeche_Mode" title="Depeche Mode">Depeche Mode</a> single, "Enjoy the Silence". In 2005, Shinoda hosted the <i>Rock Phenomenon</i> mixtape/remix CD with <a href="/wiki/DJ_Vlad" title="DJ Vlad">DJ Vlad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roc_Raida" title="Roc Raida">Roc Raida</a>. The CD is the first (and to date, only) in DJ Vlad's <i>Rock Phenomenon</i> series (which itself is a spin-off of Vlad's <i>Rap Phenomenon</i> mixtape series), and features a <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(music)" title="Mashup (music)">mashup</a> of Linkin Park's "<a href="/wiki/Papercut_(Linkin_Park_song)" title="Papercut (Linkin Park song)">Papercut</a>", and <a href="/wiki/David_Banner" title="David Banner">David Banner</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/MTA2:_Baptized_in_Dirty_Water" title="MTA2: Baptized in Dirty Water">Like a Pimp (Remix)</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-spokenhimself_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spokenhimself-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> For the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Grammy" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy">Grammy</a> awards, Shinoda and Brad Delson assembled the mashup track of "<a href="/wiki/Numb/Encore" title="Numb/Encore">Numb/Encore</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Yesterday_(Beatles_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yesterday (Beatles song)">Yesterday</a>" by <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a> to be performed live by rapper <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, Linkin Park and former <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">Beatles</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda teamed up with former bandmate Mark Wakefield to record and release a single, "Barack Your World", in October 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shinoda contributed to the music for the CNN original documentary television series, <i><a href="/wiki/This_Is_Life_with_Lisa_Ling" title="This Is Life with Lisa Ling">This Is Life with Lisa Ling</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda contributed the title theme for American television series <i><a href="/wiki/Into_the_Badlands_(TV_series)" title="Into the Badlands (TV series)">Into the Badlands</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Shinoda also created and provided the theme song for Noor Tagouri's <i>A Woman's Job</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Machine_Shop_records">Machine Shop records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Machine Shop records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Machine_Shop_Records" title="Machine Shop Records">Machine Shop Records</a></div>
<p>As Linkin Park succeeded in multi-platinum record sales, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a> granted Shinoda his own record label in 1999. It was first known as <i>The Shinoda Imprint</i>. He and bandmate Brad Delson together worked on the label in 2004 and renamed it to <a href="/wiki/Machine_Shop_Records" title="Machine Shop Records">Machine Shop Records</a>. The label signed several artists through late 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-msr_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msr-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_for_Relief" title="Music for Relief">Music for Relief</a> and <a href="/wiki/Download_to_Donate" title="Download to Donate">Download to Donate</a></div>
<p>Music for Relief is a <a href="/wiki/501(c)#501(c)(3)" class="mw-redirect" title="501(c)">501(c)(3)</a> charitable organization dedicated to providing aid to survivors of natural disasters and the prevention of such disasters through environmental programs. Music for Relief was founded by Linkin Park in response to the 2004 Indian Ocean tsunami.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Since its inception in 2005, Music for Relief has raised over $8 million for the victims of various natural disasters, including the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake">2004 Indian Ocean earthquake</a>, hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Rita" title="Hurricane Rita">Rita</a>, the <a href="/wiki/October_2007_California_wildfires" title="October 2007 California wildfires">October 2007 California wildfires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Sidr" title="Cyclone Sidr">cyclone Sidr</a> in Bangladesh, the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami">2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">hurricane Sandy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Haiyan" title="Typhoon Haiyan">typhoon Haiyan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style_and_influences">Musical style and influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Musical style and influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Shinoda was greatly inspired by both rock and hip-hop acts when he was a child. He grew up listening to <a href="/wiki/Boogie_Down_Productions" title="Boogie Down Productions">Boogie Down Productions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Enemy (group)">Public Enemy</a>, <a href="/wiki/N.W.A" title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Juice_Crew" title="Juice Crew">Juice Crew</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> and later <a href="/wiki/Nine_Inch_Nails" title="Nine Inch Nails">Nine Inch Nails</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deftones" title="Deftones">Deftones</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">the Roots</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aphex_Twin" title="Aphex Twin">Aphex Twin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Other influences and favorites of Shinoda's include <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Run-DMC" title="Run-DMC">Run-DMC</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rage_Against_the_Machine" title="Rage Against the Machine">Rage Against the Machine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purity_Ring_(band)" title="Purity Ring (band)">Purity Ring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Monkeys" title="Arctic Monkeys">Arctic Monkeys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santigold" title="Santigold">Santigold</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In an interview about his work with Linkin Park as their sound evolved over time from <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a> toward a more <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic</a> approach, Shinoda explained in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> that "We want to hopefully move even more into being able to make more substantial music. We're definitely paying attention to the substance and the nuance, and we hope to make something that's really cutting edge and really different."<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an <i>Impericon</i> interview, Shinoda stated his 'non-definitive' top three bands of all time to be Nine Inch Nails, Led Zeppelin, and <a href="/wiki/Creedence_Clearwater_Revival" title="Creedence Clearwater Revival">Creedence Clearwater Revival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Various critics have compared Shinoda's rapping style to that of fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>. A reviewer for <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> noted that Shinoda's vocals were "flowing like Eminem on <a href="/wiki/Zolpidem" title="Zolpidem">Ambien</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-Rev2_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rev2-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> An editor for <i><a href="/wiki/Uncut_(magazine)" title="Uncut (magazine)">Uncut</a></i> stated that <i>The Rising Tied</i> was "bound to please fans of Linkin Park and Eminem alike."<sup id="cite_ref-Rev2_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rev2-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Jo Timbuong of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Star_(Malaysia)" title="The Star (Malaysia)">The Star</a></i> thought "Where'd You Go" is similar to Eminem's song "<a href="/wiki/When_I%27m_Gone_(Eminem_song)" title="When I&#39;m Gone (Eminem song)">When I'm Gone</a>", noting the former as "more melancholic."<sup id="cite_ref-star_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-star-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> A reviewer of the <i><a href="/wiki/E._W._Scripps_Company" title="E. W. Scripps Company">Scripps Howard News Service</a></i> stated that Shinoda's rapping is "a smidge closer to Eminem than he is to <a href="/wiki/Vanilla_Ice" title="Vanilla Ice">Vanilla Ice</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Shinoda is a third-generation <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Americans" title="Japanese Americans">Japanese American</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sansei" title="Sansei">sansei</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> His grandfather and aunt were both interned in a <a href="/wiki/Internment_of_Japanese_Americans" title="Internment of Japanese Americans">Japanese-American internment camp</a> during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-roots_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roots-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shinoda married author Anna Hillinger in 2003, and together they have three children.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT2018_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT2018-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shinoda was awarded with the Japanese American National Museum's Award of Excellence in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-spokenhimself_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spokenhimself-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, Shinoda received an Honorary <a href="/wiki/Doctorate_of_Humane_Letters" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctorate of Humane Letters">Doctorate of Humane Letters</a> (L.H.D.) from the <a href="/wiki/Art_Center_College_of_Design" class="mw-redirect" title="Art Center College of Design">Art Center College of Design</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-spokenhimself_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spokenhimself-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/East_West_Players" title="East West Players">East West Players</a> honored him with a Visionary Award and a dinner in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-spokenhimself_131-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spokenhimself-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> In September 2012, he started writing articles for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Issue" title="The Big Issue">The Big Issue</a></i> in the UK and was the publication's <a href="/wiki/U.S._election" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. election">U.S. election</a> correspondent.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Big_Issue_September_2012_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Big_Issue_September_2012-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mike_Shinoda_discography" title="Mike Shinoda discography">Mike Shinoda discography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Shinoda_production_discography" title="Mike Shinoda production discography">Mike Shinoda production discography</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park_discography" title="Linkin Park discography">Linkin Park discography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Minor#Discography" title="Fort Minor">Fort Minor §&#160;Discography</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_Mike_Shinoda">As Mike Shinoda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: As Mike Shinoda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_Fort_Minor">As Fort Minor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: As Fort Minor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="With_Linkin_Park">With Linkin Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mike_Shinoda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: With Linkin Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Hybrid_Theory" title="Hybrid Theory">Hybrid Theory</a></i> (2000)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Meteora_(album)" title="Meteora (album)">Meteora</a></i> (2003)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Minutes_to_Midnight_(Linkin_Park_album)" title="Minutes to Midnight (Linkin Park album)">Minutes to Midnight</a></i> (2007)</li>
